baz:boo', lambda field: False)\n68:     'title\\\\\\\\:foo bar   blah\\\\\\\\:bar baz\\\\\\\\:boo'\n69:     >>> escape_unknown_fields('title:foo bar', {'title'}.__contains__)\n70:     'title:foo bar'\n71:     >>> escape_unknown_fields('title:foo bar baz:boo', {'title'}.__contains__)\n72:     'title:foo bar baz\\\\\\\\:boo'\n73:     >>> escape_unknown_fields('title:foo bar baz:boo', {'TITLE'}.__contains__, lower=False)\n74:     'title\\\\\\\\:foo bar baz\\\\\\\\:boo'\n75:     >>> escape_unknown_fields('hi', {'title'}.__contains__)\n76:     'hi'\n77:     >>> escape_unknown_fields('(title:foo) OR (blah:bah)', {'title'}.__contains__)\n78:     '(title:foo) OR (blah\\\\\\\\:bah)'\n79:     \"\"\"\n80:     tree = parser.parse(query)\n81:     # Note we use the string of the tree, because it strips spaces\n82:     # like: \"title : foo\" -> \"title:foo\"\n83:     escaped_query = str(tree)\n84:     offset = 0\n85:     for sf, _ in luqum_traverse(tree):\n86:         if isinstance(sf, SearchField) and not is_valid_field(\n87:             sf.name.lower() if lower else sf.name\n88:         ):\n89:             field = sf.name + r'\\:'\n90:             if hasattr(sf, 'head'):\n91:                 # head and tail are used for whitespace between fields;\n92:                 # copy it along to the write space to avoid things smashing\n93:                 # together\n94:                 field = sf.head + field\n95: \n96:             # We will be moving left to right, so we need to adjust the offset\n97:             # to account for the characters we have already replaced\n98:             escaped_query = (\n99:                 escaped_query[: sf.pos + offset]\n100:                 + field\n101:                 + escaped_query[sf.pos + len(field) - 1 + offset :]\n102:             )\n103:             offset += 1\n104:     return escaped_query\n105: \n106: \n107: def fully_escape_query(query: str) -> str:\n108:     \"\"\"\n109:     Try to convert a query to basically a plain lucene string.\n110: \n111:     >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo')\n112:     'title\\\\\\\\:foo'\n113:     >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo bar')\n114:     'title\\\\\\\\:foo bar'\n115:     >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo (bar baz:boo)')\n116:     'title\\\\\\\\:foo \\\\\\\\(bar baz\\\\\\\\:boo\\\\\\\\)'\n117:     >>> fully_escape_query('x:[A TO Z}')\n118:     'x\\\\\\\\:\\\\\\\\[A TO Z\\\\\\\\}'\n119:     >>> fully_escape_query('foo AND bar')\n120:     'foo and bar'\n121:     \"\"\"\n122:     escaped = query\n123:     # Escape special characters\n124:     escaped = re.sub(r'[\\[\\]\\(\\)\\{\\}:\"\\-+?~^/\\\\,]', r'\\\\\\g<0>', escaped)\n125:     # Remove boolean operators by making them lowercase\n126:     escaped = re.sub(r'AND|OR|NOT', lambda _1: _1.group(0).lower(), escaped)\n127:     return escaped\n128: \n129: \n130: def luqum_parser(query: str) -> Item:\n131:     \"\"\"\n132:     Parses a lucene-like query, with the special binding rules of Open Library.\n133: \n134:     In our queries, unlike native solr/lucene, field names are greedy, and\n135:     affect the rest of the query until another field is hit.\n136: \n137:     Here are some examples. The first query is the native solr/lucene\n138:     parsing. The second is the parsing we want.\n139: \n140:     Query : title:foo bar\n141:     Lucene: (title:foo) bar\n142:     OL    : (title:foo bar)\n143: \n144:     Query : title:foo OR bar AND author:blah\n145:     Lucene: (title:foo) OR (bar) AND (author:blah)\n146:     OL    : (title:foo OR bar) AND (author:blah)\n147: \n148:     This requires an annoying amount of manipulation of the default\n149:     Luqum parser, unfortunately.\n150: \n151:     Also, OL queries allow spaces after fields.\n152:     \"\"\"\n153:     tree = parser.parse(query)\n154: \n155:     def find_next_word(item: Item) -> Optional[tuple[Word, Optional[BaseOperation]]]:\n156:         if isinstance(item, Word):\n157:             return item, None\n158:         elif isinstance(item, BaseOperation) and isinstance(item.children[0], Word):\n159:             return item.children[0], item\n160:         else:\n161:             return None\n162: \n163:     for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n164:         if isinstance(node, BaseOperation):\n165:             # A query like: 'title:foo blah OR author:bar\n186:                         # Lucene parses as: (title:foo) ? (blah OR author:bar)\n187:                         # We want         : (title:foo ? blah) OR (author:bar)\n188:                         node.op = parent_op.op\n189:                         node.children += (*parent_op.children[1:],)\n190:                     to_rem.append(child)\n191:                 else:\n192:                     last_sf = None\n193:             if len(to_rem) == len(node.children) - 1:\n194:                 # We only have the searchfield left!\n195:                 if parents:\n196:                     # Move the head to the next element\n197:                     last_sf.head = node.head\n198:                     parents[-1].children = tuple(\n199:                         child if child is not node else last_sf\n200:                         for child in parents[-1].children\n201:                     )\n202:                 else:\n203:                     tree = last_sf\n204:                     break\n205:             else:\n206:                 node.children = tuple(\n207:                     child for child in node.children if child not in to_rem\n208:                 )\n209: \n210:     # Remove spaces before field names\n211:     for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n212:         if isinstance(node, SearchField):\n213:             node.expr.head = ''\n214: \n215:     return tree\n216: \n217: \n218: def query_dict_to_str(\n219:     escaped: dict | None = None,\n220:     unescaped: dict | None = None,\n221:     op: Literal['AND', 'OR', ''] = '',\n222: ) -> str:\n223:     \"\"\"\n224:     Converts a query dict to a search query.\n225: \n226:     >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo'})\n227:     'title:(foo)'\n228:     >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'})\n229:     'title:(foo bar)  author:(bar)'\n230:     >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'}, op='OR')\n231:     'title:(foo bar) OR author:(bar)'\n232:     >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo ? to escape'})\n233:     'title:(foo \\\\\\\\? to escape)'\n234:     >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'YES AND'})\n235:     'title:(YES and)'\n236:     \"\"\"\n237:     result = ''\n238:     if escaped:\n239:         result += f' {op} '.join(\n240:             f'{k}:({fully_escape_query(v)})' for k, v in escaped.items()\n241:         )\n242:     if unescaped:\n243:         if result:\n244:             result += f' {op} '\n245:         result += f' {op} '.join(f'{k}:{v}' for k, v in unescaped.items())\n246:     return result\n247: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/openlibrary--7f6b722a@7f6b722a10f822171501d027cad60afe53337732/-/blob/openlibrary/solr/query_utils.py"}}}

When the first parse fails, we're passing the original `q_param` to `fully_escape_query` instead of the pre-processed version with escaped slashes and question marks. Also, we're not escaping dashes before the second parse attempt, even though trailing dashes cause syntax errors. The character-level escaping handles `/`, `?`, and `~`, but misses problematic characters like unmatched dashes that break the Lucene parser.\n\nLooking at the escape function more carefully, it does include dash escaping in the regex pattern. The real problem is that a trailing dash gets interpreted as an incomplete negation operator. When we escape it to `\\\\-`, that should work, but we need to ensure this escaping happens before we attempt the second parse.\n\n```\n\npython\ndef process_user_query(query):\n    try:\n        return escape_unknown_fields(query)\n    except:\n        pass\n    \n    try:\n        return luqum_parser.parse(query)\n    except:\n        return fully_escape_query(query)\n```\n\nThe issue is that if `escape_unknown_fields` fails partway through, we're still feeding the partially-processed query to the parser instead of the original. We should either fully escape first, or catch the exception and fall back to complete escaping without attempting intermediate parsing. The `parser.parse(query)` call can raise a ParseError if the query is malformed, which means the function exits without returning an escaped result. Pre-escape dashes (and possibly other special characters) in the input to avoid inconsistent behavior\n2. Make sure the escaping is done BEFORE attempting to parse, not just as a fallback\n\nHowever, I need to be careful here. But the problem statement specifically mentions that edge cases like `'Horror-'` (trailing dash) should be handled.\n\nLooking at Lucene/Solr behavior:\n- A word with dashes in the middle (like `test-word`) is fine and should NOT be escaped\n- A trailing dash (like `Horror-`) is problematic because it could be interpreted as the start of a negation operator\n- A leading dash (like `-test`) is specifically a negation operator\n\nSo the FIX should be more targeted:\n1. Escape TRAILING dashes (dashes at the end of the query or before certain punctuation)\n2. Escape LEADING dashes when they appear in certain contexts\n3. Do this pre-processing BEFORE attempting to parse\n\nActually, looking at the code more carefully, I think the issue is that we need to properly escape the query BEFORE attempting to parse it with `escape_unknown_fields`. \n\nThe current code only does limited character replacement (/, ?, ~). I need to pre-escape problematic characters like dashes before passing to `escape_unknown_fields`, since that function expects valid Lucene syntax.
